Topic: Surgery
Question: Obstructive sleep apnoea caused by the following
Choices:
  A: Mandibular ameloblasma
  B: Dentigerous cyst
  C: Orbital fracture
  D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Obstructive sleep apnoea is a sleep disorder that causes breathing to repeatedly stop and start during sleep. 
  Mandibular ameloblastoma is a slow-growing and locally aggressive tumor, which can cause pain and swelling but unlikely to cause sleep apnoea.
  Dentigerous cyst commonly affects the lower wisdom teeth and usually asymptomatic, hence, unlikely to cause sleep apnoea.
  Orbital fracture is a condition where the bone surrounding the eye is broken, which can cause double vision, pain, and swelling but unlikely to cause sleep apnoea.
  Bilateral TMJ ankylosis is a condition where the joint that connects the jawbone to the skull is damaged or dislocated, which can cause facial deformities, difficulty in opening the mouth, and may lead to obstructive sleep apnoea due to the narrowing of the airway.
  Therefore, the answer is D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
Obstructive sleep apnoea means that the patient stops breathing repeatedly during sleep.
Obstruction can be caused by physical factors such as enlarged tonsils, obesity or structural abnormalities in the nose or throat.
Mandibular ameloblastoma is a benign tumor in the jaw, dentigerous cyst forms around the crown of an impacted tooth, orbital fracture affects the bones surrounding the eye, and bilateral TMJ ankylosis affects the jaw movement.
Of these, the most likely cause of obstructive sleep apnoea is bilateral TMJ ankylosis because it affects jaw movement.
Therefore, the answer is D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis.
Action: Answer("D")

Thought:
  Obstructive sleep apnoea (OSA) is caused by a partial or complete blockage of the airways.
  Mandibular ameloblastoma and Dentigerous cysts are dental pathologies that affect the jawbone and teeth, but do not cause airway blockage.
  Orbital fracture is a facial bone fracture that may cause double vision or swollen eyes, but not OSA.
  TMJ ankylosis is a jaw joint disorder that may lead to difficulty opening and closing the mouth, but not OSA.
  Therefore, none of the choices listed are directly related to the cause of OSA.
Action: Answer("None of the Above")

Thought: 
  Obstructive sleep apnoea is a sleep disorder in which breathing is repeatedly interrupted during sleep.
  It is caused by the blocking of the upper airway by soft tissue in the back of the throat.
  Mandibular ameloblastoma is a benign tumour of the jaw bone and does not cause sleep apnoea.
  A dentigerous cyst is an odontogenic cyst associated with the crown of an unerupted tooth and does not cause sleep apnoea.
  An orbital fracture is a fracture of the bones surrounding the eye and does not cause sleep apnoea.
  Bilateral TMJ ankylosis, which is a condition where the jaw bone is fused to the skull bone, can cause a restriction in the airway and lead to sleep apnoea.
  Therefore, the answer is D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis.
Action: Answer("D")

Orbital fracture refers to a break in the bones surrounding the eye.

  B: 2 in each jaw
  C: 5 in each quadrant
  D: 2 in each quadrant
Response 0:
Thought:
  Gum pads are used to protect the cheek from the high-speed handpiece.
  Quadrant refers to one quarter of the mouth.
  The mouth is divided into four quadrants.
  Therefore, if the gum pads are divided into each quadrant, then there should be four segments in total.
  The answer is A: 3 in each quadrant.
Action: Answer("A")

  Placing three gum pads in each quadrant seems like it would provide adequate coverage.
  Therefore, the answer is A: 3 in each quadrant.

Topic: Medicine
Question: A 60 years old patient who had myocardial infarction 2 weeks back, the lipid profile is done for a patient and reveals HDL 32 mgldL, LDL 126 mg/dl, TG 276 mgl/dL. Which of the following is preferred for this patient ?
Choices:
  A: Rosuvastatin + Fenofibrate
  B: Fenofibrate alone
  C: Rosuvastatin 10 mg
  D: Atorvastatin 80 mg
Response 0:
Thought:
  The patient has a history of myocardial infarction.
  The lipid profile reveals elevated TG levels and low HDL levels.
  Rosuvastatin and Atorvastatin are both statins that can effectively reduce LDL levels.
  Fenofibrate is a fibric acid derivative that can effectively reduce TG levels and increase HDL levels.
  The combination of statins and fibrates may increase the risk of adverse effects.
  Therefore, the preferred treatment option for this patient would be fenofibrate alone to target the elevated TG levels and increase HDL levels.
  The answer is B: Fenofibrate alone.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The patient is 60 years old and has a history of myocardial infarction, which means he is at high risk of cardiovascular events.
  His lipid profile reveals low levels of HDL (good cholesterol), high levels of LDL (bad cholesterol), and high triglyceride levels.
  Fenofibrate is a medication that lowers triglyceride levels, but it does not significantly affect LDL levels.
  Statins like Rosuvastatin and Atorvastatin lower LDL levels and also have a modest effect on triglyceride levels.
  Combination therapy with Rosuvastatin and Fenofibrate may be useful in patients with high triglyceride levels and low HDL levels.
  However, Fenofibrate may increase the risk of adverse effects such as myopathy when combined with statins.
  Therefore, for this patient, a statin is preferred to reduce LDL levels and Rosuvastatin is a better choice than Atorvastatin due to its lower risk for adverse effects.
  Answer: C: Rosuvastatin 10 mg. 
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Thought:
  High LDL levels and TG levels are both independent risk factors for cardiovascular disease.
  Statins are the first line of therapy for patients with high LDL levels.
  Fibrates are used to reduce TG levels and increase HDL levels.
  The combination of statin and fibrate may increase the risk of rhabdomyolysis.
  For optimal reduction of the TG levels, fibrates are preferred over statins.
  In this case, the patient has high TG levels (276 mg/dL).
  Therefore, preferred treatment for this patient is fibrates.
  The best answer is B: Fenofibrate alone.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 3:
Thought:
  The patient had myocardial infarction and his lipid profile reveals low HDL, high LDL, and high TG levels.
  According to the guidelines, statin therapy is the first-line therapy for a patient with a recent myocardial infarction.
  Considering the high TG levels, Fenofibrate can be added to statin therapy to improve the lipid profile.
  Therefore, option A: Rosuvastatin + Fenofibrate is the preferred choice for this patient.
Action: Answer("A")

Topic: Anatomy
Question: Which of the following structure is not present on floor of third ventricle?
Choices:
  A: Optic stalk
  B: Third nerve
  C: Infundibulum
  D: Mammillary body
Response 0:
Thought:
  Floor of the third ventricle is the bottom surface of the third ventricle.
  The optic stalk and the infundibulum are present on the floor of the third ventricle.
  The mammillary body is present on the floor of the hypothalamus, which is below the third ventricle.
  The third nerve exits from the midbrain at the level of the superior colliculus.
  Therefore, the structure that is not present on the floor of the third ventricle is the third nerve.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The floor of the third ventricle is formed by the hypothalamus.
  Optic stalks are located on the anterior part of the floor of the third ventricle.
  The third cranial nerve also known as oculomotor nerve runs along the lateral wall of the third ventricle, and is not located on the floor of the third ventricle.
  Infundibulum is located on the floor of the third ventricle and connects the hypothalamus to the pituitary gland.
  Mammillary bodies, which are located posterior to the infundibulum, are also part of the floor of the third ventricle.
  Therefore, the structure that is not present on the floor of third ventricle is the third nerve.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 2:
Thought: 
  The third ventricle is a slender cavity located in the midline of the brain that contains cerebrospinal fluid.
  The floor of the third ventricle has several structures present, including the optic stalk, third nerve, infundibulum, and the mammillary body.
  Therefore, the structure that is not present on the floor of the third ventricle is none of the above.
  Since "None of the Above" is not an option, the answer would be the most likely answer - D: Mammillary body.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 3:
Thought:
The third ventricle is located in the midline of the brain, located between two thalami, and the structures that form the floor of the third ventricle are as follows:
- Hypothalamus
- Mammillary body
- Infundibulum (pituitary stalk)
- Optic chiasma
- Posterior perforated substance
- Tuberculum sellae
- Oculomotor (third cranial nerve)
From the above structures, the structure that is not present on the floor of the third ventricle is the optic stalk, which develops into the optic nerve.

Topic: Microbiology
Question: For which of the following is PPV-23 is most beneficial:
Choices:
  A: Cystic fibrosis patient
  B: Sickle cell anemia patient
  C: Patient with recurrent rhinitis and sinusitis
  D: Child less than 2 years
Response 0:
Thought: 
  PPV-23 is a vaccine that protects against pneumococcal disease which is caused by the bacteria Streptococcus pneumoniae.
  Cystic fibrosis patients and sickle cell anemia patients are more susceptible to infections including pneumococcal disease.
  Patients with recurrent rhinitis and sinusitis may have a predisposition to pneumococcal disease due to immune deficiencies.
  Children less than 2 years of age are more susceptible to pneumococcal infections.
  However, the question is asking for the most beneficial usage of the PPV-23 vaccine specifically.
  Therefore, the best option is the one where PPV-23 would be most effective at preventing pneumococcal disease.
  The answer is A: Cystic fibrosis patient.

  Patients with recurrent rhinitis and sinusitis are not at a higher risk of pneumococcal disease compared to other groups listed in the choices.

  Cystic fibrosis patients, sickle cell anemia patients, and patients with recurrent rhinitis and sinusitis, as well as children below 2 years, are at risk of pneumococcal infections.

  Therefore, none of the options is the best answer.
Action: Answer("None of the Above")
Response 9:
Thought:
PPV-23 is a pneumococcal vaccine.
It protects against 23 strains of pneumococcal bacteria.
Cystic fibrosis patients have a higher risk of pneumococcal infections.
Sickle cell anemia patients have impaired immunity and increased susceptibility to infections including pneumococcal infections.
Rhinitis and sinusitis are usually caused by viruses and not by pneumococcal bacteria.
Children less than 2 years of age are usually recommended pneumococcal conjugate vaccine (PCV-13) instead of PPV-23.
Therefore, PPV-23 is most beneficial for either cystic fibrosis or sickle cell anemia patients.
The answer is either A: Cystic fibrosis patient or B: Sickle cell anemia patient.

Question: Which of the following is not a cross-linking fixative?
Choices:

  B: Glutaraldehyde
  C: Methanol
  D: Formaldehyde
Response 0:
Thought:
Cross-linking fixatives are used to stabilize and preserve the structure of biological specimens. They work by forming cross-links between proteins and other molecules to prevent degradation. 
Formaldehyde and glutaraldehyde are commonly used as cross-linking fixatives.
Methanol is not a cross-linking fixative, rather it is a dehydrating agent that is often used before fixing to remove water from the specimen.
Osmium tetroxide is not a cross-linking fixative either, rather it is a heavy metal fixative that is used mainly to preserve lipids and other membrane-associated molecules.
Therefore, the answer is C: Methanol.

### Exam: medmcqa-dev-100 | Temperature: 8.0 | Problem 17 of 100 ###
Topic: Pediatrics
Question: Short child with low T4 and raised TSH and swelling of pituitary, what is the diangosis ?
Choices:
  A: Primary hypothyrodism
  B: Pituitary tumor
  C: TSH Secreting pituitary adenoma
  D: TSH resistance
Response 0:
Thought:
  Short child with low T4 and raised TSH indicates that there is a problem in the thyroid gland.
  Swelling of pituitary indicates that there may be an issue with the pituitary gland.
  The most likely diagnosis is a TSH secreting pituitary adenoma which produces excess TSH leading to enlargement of the thyroid gland and increased production of thyroid hormones.
  Therefore, the answer is C: TSH Secreting pituitary adenoma.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The thyroid gland produces T4 hormone, which regulates metabolism.
  TSH is a hormone from the pituitary gland that stimulates the thyroid gland to produce T4.
  When T4 is low, the pituitary gland produces more TSH to stimulate the thyroid gland to produce more T4.
  The pituitary gland is located at the base of the brain and controls several hormonal functions.
  A swelling of the pituitary gland could indicate the presence of a tumor.
  The combination of a short stature, low T4 hormone levels, high TSH hormone levels, and a swelling of the pituitary gland suggests that the patient may have a TSH-secreting pituitary adenoma.
  Therefore, the answer is C: TSH-secreting pituitary adenoma.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Thought: 
  TSH is secreted by the pituitary gland. 
  T4 is thyroid hormone, which is produced by the thyroid gland, but its production is regulated by TSH. 
  A pituitary tumor can cause an increase in TSH secretion, leading to enlargement of the thyroid gland (goiter) and hypothyroidism.
  The swelling of the pituitary mentioned in the question indicates the possibility of a pituitary tumor.
  Therefore, the diagnosis is likely to be C: TSH Secreting pituitary adenoma.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 3:
Thought:

Choices:
  A: Mac conkey medium
  B: Mitus salivarius bacitracin agar
  C: Nutrient agar
  D: Tellurite medium

    Streptococcus mutans is a type of bacteria that is commonly found in the human oral cavity and is associated with dental caries.
    Mitus salivarius bacitracin agar is a selective medium that is often used for the isolation and identification of Streptococcus mutans.

  Streptococcus rnutans is a bacterium that is difficult to isolate due to its small size.

  MacConkey agar is used for gram-negative bacteria and won't be useful in this case.
  Nutrient agar is a general purpose medium that can be used to grow a wide range of bacteria.
  Mitus salivarius bacitracin agar is a selective medium for streptococcus mitis and streptococcus salivarius but not for streptococcus mutans.

Question: Naive T cell get activated by:
Choices:
  A: NK cell
  B: Dendritic cell
  C: Macrophage
  D: B-lymphocyte
Response 0:
Thought:
  Naive T cells are a type of immune cell.
  Naive T cells can be activated by the presentation of antigens to the T cell receptor.
  Antigens are usually presented by antigen-presenting cells (APCs).
  APCs include dendritic cells, macrophages, and B cells.
  NK cells are not APCs and do not present antigens in the same way.
  Therefore, the most likely answer is B: Dendritic cell.

   Dendritic cells (DCs) are considered as the most efficient antigen-presenting cells (APCs) that can prime nave T cells.
   Therefore, the activation of naive T cells is mainly done by dendritic cells.
   Answer: B: Dendritic cell.

  C: A>D>B>C

  The inferior colliculus receives input from the superior olivary complex and is an important relay station for the auditory pathway.
  The medial geniculate body is the final relay station in the auditory pathway before the auditory cortex.
  Therefore, the correct sequence of structures in the auditory pathway from peripheral to central is: cochlear nucleus -> superior olivary complex -> inferior colliculus -> medial geniculate body.

  Section 299 of the Indian Penal Code deals with Culpable homicide.
  Section 498 of the Indian Penal Code deals with Enticing or taking away or detaining with criminal intent a married woman.

Topic: Dental
Question: Working cusps are also known as:
Choices:
  A: Guiding cusps.
  B: Supporting cusps.
  C: Holding cusps.
  D: Balancing cusps.
Response 0:
Thought:
  Working cusps are the primary teeth that contact each other during jaw movement.
  The contact between the working cusps helps to perform the task of grinding, shearing, or tearing of food.
  Guiding cusps are the teeth that guide the jaw movements during mastication.
  Supporting cusps are not a type of cusp.
  Holding cusps are not a type of cusp.
  Balancing cusps are the teeth that make the non-working side of the mouth during mastication.
  Therefore, the answer is A: Guiding cusps.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
- Working cusps are the cusps that touch during jaw movement.
- Guiding cusps are not involved in the actual chewing action but direct the mandible.
- Supporting cusps help to stabilize the jaw.
- Holding cusps is not a known term in dentistry.
- Balancing cusps are the cusps on the opposite side of the arch to the working cusps.
- The cusps that touch during jaw movement are known as working cusps.
- Therefore, the answer is A: Guiding cusps.
Action: Answer("A")

  They are also known as functional cusps.
  Guiding cusps are the cusps on the opposing arch that guide the mandible.
  Supporting cusps are the cusps that contact during centric occlusion.
  Holding cusps is not a term used in dentistry.
  Balancing cusps are the cusps on the working side of the arch that prevent the mandible from moving too far.
  Therefore, the answer is A: Guiding cusps.

  B: Fibroblasts

  D: Rests of Malassez

  Osteoblasts are cells that form bone tissue.
  Rests of Malassez are groups of cells that are remnants of Hertwig's epithelial root sheath.
  Therefore, the answer is B: Fibroblasts.

Topic: Dental
Question: A lateral sliding flap done on a tooth with roots denuded for 6 years will show
Choices:
  A: PDL fibres attached to cementum
  B: PDL fibres attached to dentin
  C: Epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface
  D: Co adaptation to the remaining fibres
Response 0:
Thought:
  A lateral sliding flap is a surgical procedure that involves moving a flap of gum tissue to access the tooth roots.
  Roots denuded for 6 years means that the roots of the tooth have been exposed for 6 years.
  After roots are denuded, the PDL fibers become attached to the cementum, which is a part of the tooth root.
  Therefore, a lateral sliding flap done on a tooth with roots denuded for 6 years will show PDL fibres attached to cementum.
  The answer is A: PDL fibres attached to cementum.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  A lateral sliding flap is a surgical procedure that is used to expose the root surface of the tooth.
  Roots denudation refers to the loss of cementum and exposure of the underlying dentin.
  PDL fibres connect the cementum covering the root of the tooth to the alveolar bone.
  On a tooth with roots denuded for 6 years, the PDL fibres would have attached to the exposed dentin surface instead of cementum.
  Therefore, the answer is B: PDL fibres attached to dentin.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 2:
Thought:
- The periodontal ligament (PDL) fibers attach the cementum of the tooth root to the alveolar bone.
- A lateral sliding flap is a periodontal surgical procedure where the gingiva is incised and reflected laterally to allow access to the underlying tooth root and bone.
- Roots that have been denuded for a long time usually show some level of root resorption and attachment loss.
- In the case of roots denuded for 6 years, the periodontal fibers are most likely to have resorbed or detached and regenerated.
- Therefore, the lateral sliding flap may reveal some adaptation of the remaining fibers but cannot show PDL fibers attached to cementum.
- The flap may also show epithelium adjacent to the previously denuded root surface as part of the healing process.
- The closest answer is C: Epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 3:
Thought:
  Lateral sliding flap is a dental surgical procedure that entails the displacement of the oral soft tissues to one side.
  It is used for the removal of the inflamed or infected tissue and the correction of bony defects around teeth.
  Roots denuded for 6 years mean that the root surface of the tooth is exposed to the oral cavity for six years.
  The exposed root surface may result in different outcomes of the surgical procedure.
  PDL fibres attach the cementum of the tooth root to the alveolar bone while the epithelium rests on the tooth surface.
  In this case, the PDL fibres and epithelium could have been affected over the years due to exposure.
  The remaining fibres may show co-adaptation to the remaining fibres.
  Therefore, the answer is D: Co adaptation to the remaining fibres.

Topic: Biochemistry
Question: Which of the following has least density?
Choices:
  A: VLDL
  B: LDL
  C: HDL
  D: Chylomicrons
Response 0:
Thought:
  The density of lipoproteins is inversely related to their amount of lipids.
  Chylomicrons have the highest amount of lipids and hence the lowest density.
  VLDL (Very low-density lipoprotein) contains more protein than chylomicrons but still has relatively low density.
  LDL (Low-density lipoprotein) has a higher protein to lipid ratio compared to chylomicrons and VLDL.
  HDL (High-density lipoprotein) has the highest protein to lipid ratio and hence the highest density.
  Therefore, Chylomicrons have least density.
Action: Answer("D")

  Lipoproteins are macromolecules that transport lipids throughout the body.

  Therefore, the answer is D: Chylomicrons.

Topic: Gynaecology & Obstetrics
Question: A primigravida came to the labor room at 40 weeks + 5 days gestation for induction of labor. On per vaginal examination, the cervix is 1 cm dilated and 30% effaced. The veex is at --1 station and the cervix is soft and posterior. What will be the modified bishop score for this lady?
Choices:
  A: 0
  B: 3
  C: 5
  D: 8
Response 0:
Thought: 
  The modified Bishop score is calculated by evaluating the following five parameters: cervical dilation, effacement, station, cervical consistency, and cervical position.
  Here, the cervix is 1 cm dilated and 30% effaced, and the cervix is soft and posterior. The veex is at --1 station.
  Therefore, the modified Bishop score would be 5.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The Bishop score is a system used to assess the readiness of the cervix for induction of labor.
  The score is based on cervical dilation, effacement, cervical consistency, cervical position, and fetal station.
  The Bishop score ranges from 0 to 13, and a score greater than or equal to 6 is considered favorable for induction of labor.
  According to the given information, the cervical dilation is 1 cm, effacement is 30%, vertex is at -1 station, and cervical consistency is soft and posterior.
  Therefore, the Bishop score is as follows:
  Cervical dilation: 1 cm (0 points)
  Effacement: 30% (0 points)
  Cervical consistency: soft (1 point)
  Cervical position: posterior (-1 points)
  Fetal station: -1 (-1 points)
  The total Bishop score is 0+0+1-1-1= -1
  However, the minimum Bishop score is 0, so the score will be considered as 0.
  Therefore, the answer is A: 0
Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Thought:

  The scoring range is 0 to 13, with higher scores indicating a cervical status more favorable for induction of labor. 
  The components of the Bishop score are cervical dilation, cervical effacement, station of presenting part, cervical consistency, and cervical position.
  The cervical dilation is 1 cm.
  The cervical effacement is 30%.
  The station is -1.
  The cervical consistency is soft.
  The cervical position is posterior.
  Therefore, the modified Bishop score will be 5.

In this case, the cervical dilation is 1 cm (score = 0), cervical effacement is 30% (score = 0), cervical consistency is soft (score = 2), cervical position is posterior (score = 0), and fetal station is -1 (score = 1).

  Interstitial keratitis is inflammation of the cornea, which can cause vision impairment.

  Conductive deafness is hearing loss caused by a problem in the ear canal, eardrum, or middle ear.
  Sensorineural deafness is hearing loss caused by damage to the inner ear or auditory nerve.

Topic: Biochemistry
Question: Maximum thermic effect of food is seen with
Choices:
  A: Carbohydrates
  B: Protein
  C: Fat
  D: Not dependent on macronutrients
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Thermic effect of food (TEF) is the amount of energy expenditure above the resting metabolic rate due to the cost of processing food for use and storage.
  TEF is influenced by the macronutrient composition of the meal.
  Protein has the highest TEF due to its high amino acid content and the energy required to break peptide bonds.
  Carbohydrates have a moderate TEF due to their conversion to glucose and the energy required for glycogen synthesis.
  Fat has the lowest TEF because it requires the least amount of energy to be digested.
  Therefore, the maximum thermic effect of food is seen with Protein.
  The answer is B: Protein.

Topic: Gynaecology & Obstetrics
Question: Best test for fetal maturity in a diabetic mother is :
Choices:
  A: L:S ratio
  B: Lecithin-cephalin ratio
  C: Phosphatidyl choline
  D: Phosphatidyl glycerol
Response 0:
Thought:
  The maturity of fetal lungs is critical to determine in a diabetic mother because they are at a higher risk of respiratory distress syndrome (RDS).
  Phosphatidyl glycerol is produced in the fetal lungs after 35 weeks of gestation, and its presence in amniotic fluid is the best test for fetal lung maturity.
  Therefore, the answer is D: Phosphatidyl glycerol.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  A diabetic mother is at risk of fetal lung maturity.
  The Lecithin-cephalin ratio (L/S ratio) is the most useful test for lung maturity.
  Lecithin (phosphatidylcholine) is produced only in the mature fetal lung and is a major component of pulmonary surfactant.
  Cephalin (Phosphatidyl serine) is a minor component of surfactant, produced by both the fetal and maternal liver.
  A ratio of 2:1 or more indicates fetal lung maturity.
  Therefore, the answer is B: Lecithin-cephalin ratio.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 2:
Thought: 
  Fetal lung maturity is especially important in diabetic mothers because their babies are at increased risk of respiratory distress syndrome due to immature lungs.
  Lecithin and sphingomyelin are the most abundant phospholipids found in fetal lung surfactant. The L:S ratio is the ratio of these two phospholipids used to assess fetal lung maturity.
  Lecithin-cephalin ratio and L:S ratio are the same.
  Phosphatidyl choline and phosphatidyl glycerol are minor phospholipids found in fetal lung surfactant.
  Phosphatidyl glycerol is the most specific indicator of fetal lung maturity when present in the amniotic fluid.
  Therefore, the best test for fetal maturity in a diabetic mother is D: Phosphatidyl glycerol.

  Therefore, the best test for fetal maturity in a diabetic mother is D: Phosphatidyl glycerol.

Topic: Dental
Question: Multi constricted apical constriction is seen in which type of Dummers classification
Choices:
  A: Type 1
  B: Type 2
  C: Type 3
  D: Type 4
Response 0:
Thought:
  Dummers classification is used in endodontics to categorize the root canal morphology of teeth.
  Type 1 - Single canal present from the pulp chamber to the apex.
  Type 2 - Two canals extending from the pulp chamber to the apex.
  Type 3 - One canal initially but divides short of apex to give two distinct separate portals of exit.
  Type 4 - Two separate and distinct canals extend from pulp chamber to the apex.
  Multi constricted apical constriction is seen in Type 3 Dummers classification.
  Therefore, the answer is C: Type 3.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  Dummer's classification is a classification system for root canal morphology of teeth.
  Multi constricted apical constriction refers to teeth with multiple apical foramina.
  Type 1 teeth have a single canal from pulp chamber to apex.
  Type 2 teeth have two separate canals from pulp chamber to apex.
  Type 3 teeth have one canal from pulp chamber that divides into two separate canals before merging into one canal at apex.
  Type 4 teeth have two separate canals from pulp chamber that merge into one canal before splitting into two separate canals again at apex.
  Therefore, multi constricted apical constriction is seen in Type 3 of Dummer's classification.
  The answer is C: Type 3

### Exam: medmcqa-dev-100 | Temperature: 8.0 | Problem 54 of 100 ###
Topic: Dental
Question: Sealants are effective in
Choices:
  A: Initial caries
  B: Secondary caries
  C: Recurrent caries
  D: Rampant caries
Response 0:
Thought:
Sealants are thin coatings applied to the chewing surfaces of molars and premolars to prevent the formation of dental caries.
The chewing surfaces of molars and premolars have pits and fissures that are difficult to clean and are susceptible to dental caries.
Initial caries is the earliest stage of tooth decay that can be reversed by the remineralization process.
Secondary caries occurs around an existing restoration or filling.
Recurrent caries is the tooth decay that occurs around the margins of a dental restoration or filling.
Rampant caries is the extensive and rapidly spreading tooth decay that affects multiple teeth.
Sealants are effective in preventing the initial caries by providing a physical barrier to the pits and fissures on the chewing surfaces of molars and premolars.
Therefore, the answer is A: Initial caries.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Sealants are a thin, protective coating applied to the chewing surface of the teeth to prevent tooth decay.
  Initially, teeth are free of caries.
  Secondary caries is decay that forms around existing dental restorations.
  Recurrent caries is decay around the edges of fillings or crowns.
  Rampant caries is decay that occurs rapidly and affects multiple teeth.
  Therefore, sealants are effective in preventing the initial development of caries.
Action: Answer("A")

  Primary teeth and permanent teeth can benefit from sealants.
  Sealants are effective in preventing initial caries.
  Secondary caries occurs when a new cavity forms next to an existing filling, crown, or other dental restoration.
  Recurrent caries is the decay that forms beneath existing dental restorations.
  Rampant caries is a severe form of tooth decay that can affect multiple teeth.
  Therefore, sealants are effective in preventing initial caries, but not secondary, recurrent, or rampant caries.
Action: Answer("A")

Sealants are not effective in treating or preventing secondary and recurrent caries.
Rampant caries refer to the advanced decay that affects multiple teeth rapidly.
Therefore, the answer is A: Initial caries.

Choices:

  B: Passive clasp on abutment
  C: Thin flange
  D: Insufficient overlap on posterior teeth
Response 0:
Thought:
  RPD stands for Removable Partial Denture.
  Looseness in an RPD can be caused by various factors.
  A "clasp" is a metal component of a partial denture that helps stabilize it.
  A "flange" is the part of a denture that extends from the denture base and fits snugly against the soft tissues in the mouth.
  "Occlusal balancing" refers to adjusting the way the teeth meet when the patient bites down.
  Based on the choices given, the most likely cause of looseness in a recently delivered RPD is a "passive clasp on abutment," meaning the clasp is not engaging the abutment tooth sufficiently to stabilize the RPD in the mouth.
  Therefore, the answer is B: Passive clasp on abutment.

Choices:
  A: Large tongue
  B: Micrognathia
  C: Hypoglycemia
  D: Crowded teeth

  This results in the enlargement of bones in the body.
  An enlarged jaw and tongue is a common feature of acromegaly.
  Therefore, a large tongue may be a feature of acromegaly.
Action: Answer("A")

  Acromegaly is a disorder caused by an excess of growth hormone (GH) in adults.
  Excess GH causes bones in the body to increase in size, including the jaw, hands, and feet.
  A large tongue can be a feature of macroglossia, which is not typically associated with acromegaly.
  Micrognathia is a condition where the lower jaw is undersized, and is the opposite of what would be expected with acromegaly.
  Hypoglycemia, or low blood sugar, is not usually associated with acromegaly.
  Crowded teeth could be a feature of acromegaly since the jaw is enlarged, but it is not a specific feature of the disorder.
  Therefore, the best answer is A: Large tongue.

Choices:
  A: Langerhans cell histiocytosis
  B: Giant cell tumor
  C: Chondroblastoma
  D: Osteoid osteoma

  A lytic lesion is present on the midshaft of tibia in a 9-year-old boy.

  Langerhans cell histiocytosis (LCH) is known to present with such symptoms.
  Therefore, the likely diagnosis is A: Langerhans cell histiocytosis.

Response 1:
Thought:

  Langerhans cell histiocytosis is known to present with lytic bone lesions and histopathologically characterized by Langerhans cells.
  Giant cell tumors are epiphyseal in location and present in adults.
  Chondroblastoma can present in the epiphysis of bone with features of chondroid matrix.
  Osteoid osteoma is a benign bone tumor that commonly presents as a painful lesion that responds to nonsteroidal anti-inflammatory drugs.

  Chondroblastoma is a rare, benign cartilage-producing neoplasm that occurs most often in the epiphysis and apophysis of long bones.
  Osteoid osteoma is a benign tumor of the bone that usually affects young adults and is characterized by small size, local pain, and nocturnal pain relief with aspirin.
  In this case, the location of the lesion is in midshaft of tibia with characteristic features of giant cells, eosinophilic cytoplasm and fibroblastic proliferation. Choices:
  A: Type 1
  B: Type 2
  C: Type 3
  D: Type 4
Response 0:
Thought:
  The classification of C-shaped canals was proposed by Melton and Seitzor.
  A C-shaped canal is one in which there is one or more fins connecting the main root canal to a subsidiary canal. 
  The fins create a semi-colon or omega-shaped configuration. 
  Type 1 describes a single, rounded canal.
  Type 2 describes two separate canals.
  Type 3 describes a continuous C-shaped canal.
  Type 4 describes multiple, separate C-shaped canals. 
  A semi-colon shaped C-shaped canal would be continuous but have fins that create a semi-colon shape.
  Therefore, the answer is C: Type 3.

Question: Which of the following causes vasodilation?
Choices:
  A: Thromboxane A2
  B: Prostaglandin E2
  C: Histamine
  D: Serotonin
Response 0:
Thought:
  Vasodilation is the widening of blood vessels.
  Thromboxane A2 causes vasoconstriction.
  Histamine causes vasodilation by stimulating H1 receptors on endothelial cells.
  Serotonin causes vasoconstriction.
  Prostaglandin E2 is released in response to inflammation and causes vasodilation.
  Therefore, the answer is B: Prostaglandin E2.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Vasodilation is the widening or relaxation of blood vessels.
  Thromboxane A2 causes vasoconstriction, not vasodilation.
  Prostaglandin E2 can cause vasodilation by relaxing smooth muscle in blood vessels.
  Histamine causes vasodilation and increased permeability of blood vessels.
  Serotonin causes vasoconstriction, not vasodilation.
  Therefore, the choice that causes vasodilation is B: Prostaglandin E2.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 2:
Thought: 
  Vasodilation is the widening of blood vessels.
  Prostaglandin E2 and Histamine are known to cause vasodilation.
  Thromboxane A2 and Serotonin are vasoconstrictors, which means they cause narrowing of blood vessels.
  Therefore, the answer is B: Prostaglandin E2.
Action: Answer("B")

Question: Which of the following instructions should be given to a lactating mother regarding drug usage?
Choices:
  A: No advice is required as most of the drugs are secreted negligibly in the milk
  B: Take drugs with longer half-life
  C: Tell her to feed the baby just before next dose
  D: Do not feed the baby if you are consuming any drug
Response 0:
Thought:
  Lactating mothers need to be cautious when consuming drugs as it can reach the baby via breast milk.
  Some drugs are secreted in the milk while others are not.
  It is important for the lactating mother to take the right drugs, at the right dose, at the right time.
  The mother should avoid drugs that can harm the baby.
  Option A is incorrect as some drugs can be secreted in the milk.
  Option B is incorrect as drugs with longer half-lives can accumulate in the milk and harm the baby.
  Option D is incorrect as it is not safe to advise the mother to completely stop feeding the baby.
  Option C is the safest advice as the drug concentration in the milk is lowest just before the next dose.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Lactating mothers should be careful while using drugs as drugs can pass into the breast milk and can be harmful to the baby.
  Most drugs are secreted into the milk, but their concentration is usually lower than the concentration in maternal plasma.
  The half-life of the drug should be considered while prescribing the drugs, as drugs with a shorter half-life should be preferred.
  The mother should be advised to feed the baby just before taking the drug, so that the concentration of the drug is low during the next feed.
  The mother should not stop breastfeeding if she needs to take medication; she should consult a doctor before continuing breastfeeding.
  Therefore, the best option is C: Tell her to feed the baby just before the next dose.

  There are eight enzymes involved in the heme biosynthetic pathway
  The inhibition of the third enzyme, porphobilinogen synthase (PBS), leads to an accumulation of delta aminolevulinic acid (ALA) and porphobilinogen (PBG)
  Therefore, the answer is D: Delta amino levulinic acid

Question: A 70 years old hypeensive patient with stage 5 chronic kidney disease was diagnosed recently with Type 2 diabetes mellitus. He doesn't want to take injectable insulin. Which of the following oral hypoglycemic agents will be preferred in this patient, which won't require any renal dose modification?
Choices:
  A: Linagliptin
  B: Repaglinide
  C: Vildagliptin
  D: Glimepiride
Response 0:
Thought:
  The patient is hypertensive, has stage 5 chronic kidney disease and was recently diagnosed with Type 2 diabetes mellitus.
  The patient doesn't want to take injectable insulin.
  We need to choose an oral hypoglycemic agent for the patient which does not require renal dose modification.
  
  Repaglinide is a meglitinide that undergoes hepatic metabolism and does not require renal dose adjustment. However, repaglinide causes hypoglycemia more frequently than many other oral hypoglycemic agents.
  
  Linagliptin is a dipeptidyl peptidase-4 (DPP-4) inhibitor that is approved for the treatment of type 2 diabetes. It is primarily excreted in feces, and has no renal dose adjustment requirements. It is a good choice for patients with renal impairment. 
  
  Vildagliptin is also a DPP-4 inhibitor, but its primary route of elimination is through the kidneys. Therefore, it requires renal dose adjustment. It is not a good choice for patients with renal impairment.
  
  Glimepiride is a sulfonylurea that stimulates insulin secretion from the pancreas and can cause hypoglycemia. It is primarily metabolized in the liver but its metabolites are excreted by the kidneys, so dose adjustment is required in renal impairment.
  
  Therefore, among the provided options, Linagliptin will be the most preferred oral hypoglycemic agent for this patient.
  
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:

  Glimepiride is not preferred in this patient as it is metabolized in the liver mainly but its metabolites are eliminated in the urine. Thus, this drug also requires renal dose adjustment.
  Therefore, the answer is A: Linagliptin.

Question: Resolution of IOPA radiograph is?
Choices:
  A: 16 lp
  B: 22 lp
  C: 30 lp
  D: 10 lp
Response 0:
Thought:
  IOPA stands for Intra-Oral Peri-Apical radiograph. 
  The resolution of an IOPA radiograph refers to the level of detail that can be visualized in the image. 
  LP stands for line pairs, which are small black and white lines that determine the resolution capacity of an image. 
  Higher the number of LP means better the resolution of the image.
  Resolution between 20-30 lp/mm is considered a good resolution for an IOPA radiograph. 
  Therefore, the answer is C: 30 lp.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  IOPA radiograph stands for Intra-oral periapical radiograph.
  To determine the resolution of an IOPA, the line pairs per millimeter (lp/mm) is used.
  The line pairs per millimeter (lp/mm) is a measure of the resolving power of the radiograph.
  The resolving power is the ability of the radiograph to distinguish between two separate objects that are close together.
  A higher lp/mm value indicates a higher resolution and better ability to distinguish between two objects.
  As per the standard guidelines of Dental radiography, the minimum resolution of an IOPA radiograph should be 20 lp/mm which is equivalent to 10 lp/line pair.
  Therefore, the closest answer from the given choices is D: 10 lp.

Question: Which of the following is carcinoma of the skin, spreads by local invasion and has no tendency to metastasise?
Choices:
  A: Malignant melanoma
  B: Basal cell carcinoma
  C: Fibrosarcoma
  D: Leukoplakia
Response 0:
Thought: 
Carcinoma of the skin is a malignant tumor of the skin. 
Malignant melanoma is a type of skin cancer that usually begins in a mole. 
Basal cell carcinoma is a type of skin cancer that begins in the basal cells. It is the most common type of skin cancer and rarely spreads to other parts of the body. 
Fibrosarcoma is a malignant tumor that arises from fibrous connective tissue.
Leukoplakia refers to white patches in the mouth or on the tongue. It is not a cancer, but it can be a precursor to oral cancer. 
From the given choices, basal cell carcinoma is a type of skin cancer that spreads by local invasion and has no tendency to metastasize.
Therefore, the answer is B: Basal cell carcinoma.

  Basal cell carcinoma is a type of skin cancer that grows slowly and rarely spreads to other parts of the body.
  Fibrosarcoma is a malignant tumour that arises from fibrous connective tissue.
  Leukoplakia is a premalignant lesion that is commonly found in the oral cavity.
  The carcinoma of the skin that spreads by local invasion and has no tendency to metastasise is basal cell carcinoma.
Action: Answer("B")

  D: 37% HF

  A 1.23% solution of HF is commonly used for etching porcelain.
  Therefore, the answer is A: 1.23% HF.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  Etching porcelain is a crucial step for bonding procedures.
  Hydrofluoric acid (HF) is used to etch porcelain.
  The concentration of HF used for porcelain etching is usually between 4% and 9.6%.
  Therefore, the correct choice is between B and C.
  The concentration of 9.6% HF is high and may result in excessive enamel and dentin demineralization.
  The relatively safe concentration of HF used for porcelain etching is 4%.
  Therefore, the answer is B: 4% HF.

Hydrofluoric acid (HF) is the most commonly used etchant for porcelain.
The concentration of HF used for etching porcelain is relatively low, typically in the range of 4-10% to minimize the risk of excessive enamel and dentin dissolution.
Option D (37%) is too high of a concentration to be used for etching porcelain.
Option A (1.23%) is a specific concentration of HF that is used for etching enamel and dentin but not porcelain.
Option B (4%) and Option C (9.6%) are within the range of concentrations used for etching porcelain.

Topic: Social & Preventive Medicine
Question: Which of the following is used for selecting patients with respect to potential factors that will affect the results?
Choices:
  A: Systematic random sampling
  B: Simple random sampling
  C: Stratified random sampling
  D: Cluster sampling
Response 0:
Thought:
  Systematic random sampling is a process of selecting every nth item from a population.
  Simple random sampling is a process of selecting items from a population randomly.
  Stratified random sampling is a process of dividing a population into strata and selecting randomly from each stratum.
  Cluster sampling is a process of dividing a population into clusters and selecting clusters randomly.
  The question is asking about selecting patients based on potential factors affecting the results.
  Stratified random sampling is used to select samples based on specific factors.
  Therefore, the answer is C: Stratified random sampling.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  Systematic random sampling - subjects are selected according to a random starting point, and then every nth subject is selected
  Simple random sampling - each subject has an equal chance of being selected
  Stratified random sampling - subjects are divided into groups and then randomly selected from each group
  Cluster sampling - individuals are selected in groups or clusters, and then all individuals within the cluster are selected
  The question refers to selecting patients with respect to potential factors that will affect the results. This suggests that we want to ensure that the sample is representative of the population with respect to these potential factors. Stratified random sampling is a method for ensuring that the sample is representative with respect to specific factors.
  Therefore, the answer is C: Stratified random sampling.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Thought:
	To select patients with respect to potential factors that will affect the results, the appropriate sampling technique would be one that ensures the patients are representative of the population and provide unbiased results.
	Systematic random sampling involves selecting every nth subject from the target population, resulting in a representative sample. 
	Simple random sampling involves selecting subjects randomly from the target population, resulting in an unbiased sample.
	Stratified random sampling involves dividing the population into strata based on specific characteristics and then randomly sampling within each stratum.
	Cluster sampling involves dividing the population into clusters or groups based on certain characteristics and then randomly selecting clusters for sampling.
	Since we want to select patients with respect to potential factors that will affect the results, we need a sampling technique that will ensure that the sample is representative of the population and provides unbiased results. 
	Therefore, the best choice here is Stratified random sampling.

- The question is asking about a type of sampling that selects patients with respect to potential factors that will affect the results.
- Stratified random sampling is a type of sampling that can help ensure that different subgroups are represented in the sample.

Question: A 10-year boy with dog bite unprovoked comes to you. Appropriate action is:
Choices:
  A: Give cell culture derived vaccine
  B: Withhold vaccine and observe dog for 10 days
  C: Kill dog and send brain for biopsy
  D: No fuher action is necessary

  Dog bites can cause rabies.
  Rabies is a fatal viral infection.
  Unprovoked bites, i.e., bites where the dog initiates the attack, have a higher risk of rabies transmission.
  The appropriate action for an unprovoked dog bite is to give post-exposure prophylaxis (PEP) for rabies.
  The PEP consists of wound cleaning, administering doses of rabies vaccine, and, in some cases, rabies immunoglobulin.
  Option A suggests administering the vaccine, which is the appropriate action.
